Jamison Brereton

112
A┼Ыvins (except Heaven and Earth 1a, Agni 1b) Kutsa ─Ас╣Еgirasa
25 verses: jagat─л, except triс╣гс╣нubh 24тАУ25
This tightly structured hymn conforms to the list format frequently found in A┼Ыvin hymns. A p─Бda-length refrain ends every verse but the last two (24тАУ25), urging the A┼Ыvins to come with the same forms of help they have used in past rescues and marvelous deeds. The first three quarters of each verse provides examples of said deeds; as often in A┼Ыvin hymns, many of these involve little-known or unknown episodes and proper names of otherwise unidentified clients of the A┼Ыvins, inter
mixed with allusions to myths and legends found at least glancingly elsewhere. This fast-moving catalogue occupies most of the hymn (starting especially with vs. 5, through vs. 23), and its effect is to convince the audience that, with so many helpful interventions behind them, the A┼Ыvins will surely answer our calls for help, as finally articulated in vss. 24тАУ25.

The beginning of the hymn (vss. 1тАУ4), while the rhetorical pattern is still being estab lished, is more difficult and more syntactically and conceptually dense. The climax of this portion of the hymn is verse 4, where the rhetorical pattern gets its full shape but the content has not yet settled into the litany that follows. The pervasive double mean ing of verse 4 cannot be conveyed directly in translation, for each part of the verse, on the one hand, identifies an unnamed divinity associated with the early-morning sacri fice (Wind [V─Бyu], Agni, and Soma) by characteristic epithets, while, on the other, all three descriptions are also appropriate to the A┼ЫvinsтАЩ chariot (already mentioned in vs. 2), on which they will make the journey constantly alluded to in the refrain.

Jamison Brereton Notes

A┼Ыvins On the structure of the hymn, see the published introduction. The challenging verses are the first four. I will not comment on the many obscure mythic fragments that constitute the A┼ЫvinsтАЩ various rescues, nor attempt to etymologize the many personal names.

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬI praise Heaven and Earth for preliminary meditation, (prior to the coming of the A┼Ыvins); I praise the hot and bright-shining Agni upon their approach, (as preparatory) to their worship; with those appliances with which you sound the conch-shell in battle for your share (in the booty), with those aids, A┼Ыvins, come willingly hither.тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

Utibhiс╕е, instrumental plural of uti, help, aid, assistance, protection; hence, without those aids

Jamison Brereton

I reverently invoke Heaven and Earth, to be first in their thought; (I reverently invoke) Agni and the very bright gharma drink, for (the
A┼Ыvins) to seek on their journey.
Those with which you stimulate the decisive act in the match, for (us to gain) a shareтАФwith those forms of help come here, o A┼Ыvins.

Jamison Brereton Notes

p┼лrv├бcitti- is variously interpreted and much discussed: see the long notes of Geldner and Renou ad loc., as well as Oldenberg, KlSch 1152-56 (=NG 1916). The stem always occurs in the dat. and displays (quasi-)infinitival usage. Although it would be possible to take it as тАЬ(for me/us) to think first (of them)тАЭ and in the first p─Бda of a hymn this would be easily interpretable as a ritual reference, I consider it to have the opposite value: тАЬ(for them) to think first (of me/us).тАЭ Kutsa repeatedly calls on Heaven and Earth to be witness to his speech in the refrain of I.105: vitt├бm me asy├б rodas─л. Cf. also X.35.1 mah─л╠Бdy─Б╠Бv─Бprthiv ╠е ─л╠Бcetat─Бm ├бpaс╕е тАЬLet great Heaven and Earth take cognizance of (our) work.тАЭ For further on p┼лrv├бcittaye see comm. ad IX.99.5.

The stem iс╣гс╣н├н- is a perennial problem, since it can belong to several different roots: тИЪiс╣г тАШdesire, seekтАЩ, тИЪiс╣г тАШsend, impelтАЩ, or тИЪyaj тАШsacrificeтАЩ. Geldner (n. 1b) takes it here to an intransitive iс╣г тАШrasch, gern willig kommen, eilenтАЩ, though his tr. тАШsich beeilenтАЩ might seem to connect it with a reflexive sense of тАШsend, impelтАЩ. By isolating iс╣гс╣н├бye from the acc. gharm├бm, he then needs to supply another verb to govern that acc., namely тАЬ(zu kochen).тАЭ Oldenberg (KlSch 282-84 [=ZDMG 62 (1908)]), however, gives good reasons to connect our iс╣гс╣н├бye with тАШseekтАЩ, though his interpr. of this p─Бda differs somewhat from mine. So also Renou (see his n.). Witzel Got┼Н opt for тАШsendтАЩ.

Griffith

To give first thought to them, I worship Heaven and Earth, and Agni, fair bright glow, to hasten their approach.
Come hither unto us, O Asvins, with those aids wherewith in fight ye speed the war-cry to the spoil.

Geldner

Himmel und Erde rufe ich auf, um ihrer zuerst zu gedenken; ich rufe Agni, den Glanzreichen, den hei├Яen Trank zu kochen, auf da├Я die Asvin in ihrer Fahrt sich beeilen. Mit den Hilfen, mit denen ihr im Kampfe unserem Einsatz zum Siege verhelfet - mit diesen Hilfen kommt doch ja her, ihr Asvin!

Grassmann

Zur ersten Andacht preise Erd’ und Himmel ich, die lichte Glut, den Agni, dass er eilig komm’; Mit solchen H├╝lfen kommt, o Ritter, schnell herbei, durch die im Kampf den Streiter ihr zur Beute f├╝hrt.

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬEarnest and exclusive adorers stand, A┼Ыvins, round your car, (to benefit) by your bounty, as (disciples listen) to the words (of a teacher) for instrumental uction; with those aids with which you defend the pious who are engaged in acts of worship, come, A┼Ыvins,wilingly hither.тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

For you two to give them, inexhaustible (gifts?), easy to carry, have mounted onto your chariot, as if onto an eloquent (vehicle) for
thinking.
Those with which you help (us) to seek insights at the cultic actтАФwith those forms of help come here, o A┼Ыvins.

Jamison Brereton Notes

This verse is very dense and has been subject(ed) to a variety of interpretations, the details of which canтАЩt be laid out here. The first hemistich depicts gifts or some other desirable things mounting the chariot of the A┼Ыvins to be given.

The gifts are qualified as subh├бr─Бс╕е тАШeasy to carry (away?)тАЩ and тАШinexhaustibleтАЩ (asa┼Ыcat├бс╕е); the latter word generally qualifies тАШstreamsтАЩ, objects that are not ordinarily capable of mounting anything. This already odd image (of gifts [implicitly compared to streams] performing the mounting) is made odder by the simile in b, which compares the chariot to something eloquent (vacas├бm) for thinking (m├бntave).

It is of course not unusual for a verbal product (a hymn vel sim.) to be compared to a chariot, but the semantic distance traversed in this hemistich is quite far. This outr├й simile referring to the chariot may anticipate 4c below.

I wonder if the hapax thematic vacas├б- (in acc. vacas├бm) is wrongly accented for *vac├бsam, which could be an internally derived possessive adj. to the neut. s-stem v├бcas- тАШspeechтАЩ. Although this putative *vac├бs- тАШhaving speech, eloquentтАЩ would likewise be a hapax, it would belong to a standard derivational type. BR (and Monier-Williams) take just this word as a derivative of тИЪva├▒c тАШmove waveringlyтАЩ, which certainly would better fit a chariot. But the following the following m├бntave strongly favors a derivative of тИЪvac, given the common conjunction of thought and speech.

The final phrase of c, k├бrman iс╣гс╣н├бye echoes that of 1b y─Б╠Бman iс╣гс╣н├бye, and the two forms of iс╣гс╣н├бye should therefore be interpreted in the same way. I take dh├нyaс╕е тАШinsightsтАЩ as the object of the seeking and supply тАЬ(us)тАЭ as the subject of the infinitive.

Others tr., with different interpretations of iс╣гс╣н├бye, have taken different routes.

Griffith

Ample, unfailing, they have mounted as it were an eloquent car that ye may think of us and give.
Come hither unto us, O Asvins, with those aids wherewith ye help our thoughts to further holy acts.

Geldner

Auf eurem Wagen stellten sich zum Verschenken die leichtlastenden unversieglichen Gaben ein wie bei einem Wortkundigen die Gedanken zum Ersinnen sich einstellen. Mit denen ihr Asvin die Gedanken f├╢rdert, da├Я sie bei der heiligen Handlung willig kommen - mit diesen Hilfen kommt doch ja her, ihr Asvin!

Grassmann

F├╝r eure Huld bestiegen wuchtig unersch├╢pft den Wagen H├╝lfen, dass er fast zu wanken scheint, Mit solchen H├╝lfen kommt, o Ritter, schnell herbei, mit denen Andacht ihr beeilt beim heil’gen Werk.

рдкрджрд╛рд░реНрдерд╛рдиреНрд╡рдпрднрд╛рд╖рд╛рдГ - (рдпреБрд╡реЛрдГ) рдпреБрд╡рдпреЛрдГ (рджрд╛рдирд╛рдп) рд╕реБрдЦрд╡рд┐рддрд░рдгрд╛рдп (рд╕реБрднрд░рд╛рдГ) рдпреЗ рд╕реБрд╖реНрдареБ рднрд░рдиреНрддрд┐ рдкреБрд╖реНрдгрдиреНрддрд┐ рд╡рд╛ (рдЕрд╕рд╢реНрдЪрддрдГ) рдЕрд╕рдорд╡реЗрддрд╛рдГ (рд░рдердореН) рд░рдордгрд╕рд╛рдзрдирдВ рдпрд╛рдирдореН (рдЖ) (рддрд╕реНрдереБрдГ) рддрд┐рд╖реНрдардиреНрддрд┐ (рд╡рдЪрд╕рдореН) рд╕рд░реНрд╡реИрдГ рд╕реНрддреБрддреНрдпрд╛ рдкрд░рд┐рднрд╛рд╖рд┐рддрдВ рдордиреБрд╖реНрдпрдореН (рди) рдЗрд╡ (рдордиреНрддрд╡реЗ) рд╡рд┐рдЬреНрдЮрд╛рддреБрдореН (рдпрд╛рднрд┐рдГ) (рдзрд┐рдпрдГ) рдкреНрд░рдЬреНрдЮрд╛рдГ (рдЕрд╡рдердГ) рд░рдХреНрд╖рдердГ (рдХрд░реНрдордиреН) рдХрд░реНрдордгрд┐ (рдЗрд╖реНрдЯрдпреЗ) рдЗрд╖реНрдЯрд╕реБрдЦрд╛рдп (рддрд╛рднрд┐рдГ) (рдЙ) (рд╕реБ) (рдКрддрд┐рднрд┐рдГ) (рдЕрд╢реНрд╡рд┐рдирд╛) рд╡рд┐рджреНрдпрд╛рджрд┐рджрд╛рддрд╛рд░рд╛рд╡рдзреНрдпрд╛рдкрдХреЛрдкрджреЗрд╢рдХреМ (рдЖ) рд╕рдордиреНрддрд╛рддреН (рдЧрддрдореН) рдкреНрд░рд╛рдкреНрдиреБрддрдореН рее реи рее

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬBy the vigour infused from celestial nectar, you are able, leaders (of sacrifice), to rule over those beings (who people the three worldds); with those aids by which you gave (milk) to the barren cow, come, A┼Ыvins, willingly hither.тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

Legend: To the cow of a с╣Ыс╣гi, named ┼Ъayu, to which, although barren, the A┼Ыvins, at his entreaty, gave abundance of milk

Jamison Brereton

You two rule over these clans at the command of the divine, through the might of the immortal.
Those with which you swell the uncalved cow, you superior menтАФwith those forms of help come here, o A┼Ыvins.

Jamison Brereton Notes

The phrase divy├бsya pra┼Ы─Б╠Бsane can be read in (at least) two different ways: either the A┼Ыvins are тАЬin commandтАЭ of the divine (that is, they command the divine) or тАЬat the commandтАЭ of the divine (that is, the divine gives them the command). I follow Geldner in taking it as the latter; he cleverly suggests that this shows the A┼Ыvins in their proper position between gods and men – in other words, they are middle management.

Griffith

Ye by the might which heavenly nectar giveth you are in supreme dominion Lords of all these folk.
Come hither unto us, O Asvins, with those aids wherewith ye, Heroes, made the barren cow give milk.

Geldner

Ihr habt auf Gehei├Я des himmlischen Geschlechts ├╝ber diese St├дmme die Macht kraft eures Lebensbalsams. Mit denen ihr die unfruchtbare Kuh milchreich macht, ihr Herren, - mit diesen Hilfen kommt doch ja her, ihr Asvin!

Grassmann

Mit Herrscherkraft beherrschet diese St├дmme ihr im Machtgebiet des himmlischen Unsterblichen; Mit solchen H├╝lfen kommt, o Ritter, schnell herbei, durch die die unfruchtbare Kuh ihr schwellen lasst.

Elizarenkova

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬWith those aids by which the circumambient (wind), endowed with the vigour of his son, the measurer of the two worlds (of heaven and earth), and swiftest of the swift, beautifies (all things), and by which (Kakс╣г─лvat) became learned in the three kinds of sacrifice; with them come, A┼Ыvins, willingly hither.тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

Endowed with the vigour of his son: Agni is the son of Va-yu; v─Бyor-agniс╕е (Taittir─лya ─Аraс╣Зyaka 8.1), either as genitive rated, in the character of digestive warmth, by the vital airs, or as having been excited into flame by the wind at the time of creation; Measurer of the two world: dv─лm─Бtс╣Ы may relate to the wind inconjunction with Agni, as the occupants of the firmament and the earth, respectively; or, explained as the son of two mothers, or the two sticks used for attrition, and hence, applicable to Agni; Learned in the three kinds of sacrifice: Or, trimantu, acquaintd with the p─Бka-yaj├▒as, or offering sof food; the havir yaj├▒as, or oblations of clarified butter, and the soma yaj├▒as, or libations of Soma. Trimantu = Kakс╣г─лvat

Jamison Brereton

Those through which the earth-encircler [=Wind] is distinguished in the might of his extension, through which he of two mothers [=Agni] is distinguished, transiting in his transits,
through which the wide-gazing one [=Soma] became of triple thoughtтАФ with those forms of help come here, o A┼Ыvins.

Jamison Brereton Notes

As discussed in the published introduction, this verse seems to display extended double reference between three gods associated with the morning pressing and the A┼ЫvinsтАЩ chariot, an association produced by shared epithets, though I must admit that there are many loose ends in this interpretation. See also RenouтАЩs n.

In p─Бda a p├бrijman- тАШearth-encirclerтАЩ is a standard epithet of their chariot (I.20.3, IV.45.1, X.39.1, X.41.1, IV.3.6)(and, in the dual, of the A┼Ыvins themselves: I.46.14, X.106.3). In a verse in an A┼Ыvin hymn in which this is the first real word, it is hard to imagine that an audience would not first think of their chariot. However, the term also qualifies the Wind (e.g., VII.40.6, II.38.2), and the rest of p─Бda a, t├бnayasya majm├бn─Б, fits a divinity better than a chariot.

In its other three occurrences dvim─Бt├бr- тАШhaving two mothersтАЩ refers to Agni, as produced by the two kindling sticks. It is somewhat difficult to see how this word could refer to the chariot, unless the A┼Ыvins are configured as two mothers. On the other hand the phrase dh┼лrс╣г├║ tar├бс╣Зayaс╕е, like our t┼лrс╣г├║ tar├бс╣Зiс╕е, is found in an A┼Ыvin hymn (VII.6.78) qualifying their horses in a verse also containing their chariot. (Cf. also tar├бс╣Зi- twice in another A┼Ыvin hymn [IV.45.5, 7], but used of a priest, probably Agni.) Note also that t┼лrс╣г├║ not only plays on the dh┼лrс╣г├║ in the passage just cited, but also phonologically matches the ┼л с╣г├║ of this hymnтАЩs refrain.

In c vicakс╣гan├б- тАШwide-gazingтАЩ is otherwise esp. found as an epithet of Soma, though occasionally of other gods. As a qualifier of a chariot, it could mean тАШconspicuousтАЩ (тЖР тАШwidely seenтАЩ). What it would mean for either Soma or the chariot to be тАШof triple thoughtтАЩ (trim├бntu-) is not clear to me. The word is a hapax, but it should be interpreted along with the m├бntave of 2b, where the word is connected with an image (however attenuated) of a chariot. ItтАЩs worth keeping in mind that the A┼ЫvinsтАЩ chariot is characterized as having three of everything in I.34.2, 9, 12, and its three wheels are mentioned elsewhere. As for a potential connection with Soma, the тАШthreeтАЩ of course suggests the three soma pressings, though exactly what the -m├бntuwould have to do with them isnтАЩt clear to me. Perhaps more likely is the three types of ritual speech deployed in the soma sacrifice.

Note that there is an implicit numerical ordering of the subjects of the three p─Бdas: (p├бrijman = 1), dvim─Бt├бr-, trim├бntu-.

In sum, although the vocabulary of this verse has tantalizing resonances with other passages and although I am fairly certain there is a pervasive double meaning, I do not feel I (or anyone else) has entirely тАЬcrackedтАЭ this verse. The tack taken by Geldner (/Witzel Got┼Н) of simply taking Parijman, Dvim─Бtar, and Trimantu as PNs is the easy way out but does not advance the interpretation.

Griffith

The aids wherewith the Wanderer through his offspring’s might, or the Two-Mothered Son shows swiftest mid the swift;
Wherewith the sapient one acquired his triple lore,–Come hither unto us, O Asvins, with those aids.

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬWith those aids by which you raised up from the water, Rebha, who had been cst bound (into a well), and also Vandana (similarly circumstanced), to behold the sky; by which you protected Kaс╣Зva, when longing to see the light; with them, A┼Ыvins, come willingly hither.тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

Legends: Rebha and Vandana are с╣Ыс╣гis who were cast into wells by the asuras. Kaс╣Зva threw them into darkness

Jamison Brereton

Those with which from the waters you raised up rasping Rebha, who was confined and bound, and raised up Vandana to see the sun,
with which you helped Kaс╣Зva desiring gainтАФwith those forms of help come here, o A┼Ыvins.

Jamison Brereton Notes

In тАЬrasping RebhaтАЭ (rebh├б-) I have incorporated the gloss into the name. The word occurs in the next hymn (I.113.17) in its lexical meaning.

Griffith

Wherewith ye raised from waters, prisoned and fast bound, Rebha, and Vandana to look upon the light;
Wherewith ye succoured Kanva as he strove to win,–Come hither unto us, O Asvins, with those aids.

Geldner

Mit denen ihr den gefangnen, gefesselten Rebha aus dem Wasser den Vandana herausholtet, um die Sonne wiederzusehen, mit denen ihr dem auf Verdienst ausgehenden Kanva weiterhalft - mit diesen Hilfen kommt doch ja her, ihr Asvin!

Grassmann

Durch die ihr Rebha, der gebunden und verh├╝llt, aus Fluten zogt, und Vandana, das Licht zu schaun, Durch die ihr Kanva halfet, dem verlangenden, mit solchen H├╝lfen kommt, o Ritter, schnell herbei.

Elizarenkova

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬWith those aids by which you rescued Antaka, (when cast into) a deep (pool), and about to be destroyed; by which, inflicting no distress, you preserved Bhujyu, and by which you relieved Karkandhu and Vayya; with them, A┼Ыvins, come willingly hither.тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

Antaka was a r─Бjarс╣гi, whom the asuras threw into a pond or a well;

Bhujyu = son of R─Бj─Б Tugra. Bhujyu had embarked on a maritime expedition against the enemies of his father, but encountered a storm, in which his vessel was lost; he was saved, and brught back to his father by the intervention of the A┼Ыvins; Karkabandhu and Vayya: asuras whom the A┼Ыvins extricated from isfortunes; cf. RV. I.116.3

Jamison Brereton

Those with which you revived Antaka, languishing in foreign parts, with which unwavering ones you revived Bhujyu,
with which you revive Karkandhu and VayyaтАФwith those forms of help come here, o A┼Ыvins.

Jamison Brereton Notes

On ─Б╠Бraс╣Зa- see comm. on VIII.70.8.

Griffith

Wherewith ye rescued Antaka when languishing deep in the pit, and Bhujyu with unfailing help.
And comforted Karkandhu, Vayya, in their woe,–Come hither unto us, O Asvins, with those aids.

Geldner

Mit denen ihr den in der Grube verschmachtenden Antaka, mit welchen nie irregehenden Hilfen ihr den Bhujyu erquickt habt, mit denen ihr den Karkandhu und Vayya erquicket - mit diesen Hilfen kommt doch ja her, ihr Asvin!

Grassmann

Mit welchen sichern H├╝lfen ihr dem Antaka, dem in der Tiefe schmachtenden und Bhudschju halft, Durch die Karkandhu und den Vajja ihr erquickt, mit solchen H├╝lfen kommt, o Ritter, schnell herbei.

Elizarenkova

тАЬWith those aids by which you enriched ┼Ъucanti, and gave him a handsome habitation, and rendered the scorching heat plural asurable to Atri, and by which you preserved Pс╣Ы┼Ыnigu and Purukutsa; with them, A┼Ыvins, come willingly hither.тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

Atri, the patriarch, was thrown by the asuras into a cave with a hundred doors, at all of which fires of chaff were kindled; the fires were extinguished with cold water by the A┼Ыvins; or, Atri = Agni, the eater (attri)of clarified butter, but whose appetite, or intensity, being checked by the heat of the sun in the hot weather, was renovated by the rain sent down by the A┼Ыvins. Pс╣Ыс╣гnigu = pс╣Ыс╣гс╣Зayo g─Бvo yasya, so named from possessing bridled cows

English translation:

тАЬWith those aids by which you enabled the opulent Vi┼Ыpal─Б, when she was unable to move, to go to the battle rich in a thousand spoils, and by which you protected the devout Va┼Ыa, the son of A┼Ыva; with them, A┼Ыvins, come willingly hither.тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

Vi┼Ыpal─Б was the wife of Khela, son of Agastya. Va┼Ыa and Asva were с╣Ыс╣гis

Jamison Brereton

Those with which you revived Vi┼Ыpal─Б, to pursue the way, to gain the stakes in the contest with a thousand battle-prizes,
with which you helped Va┼Ыa A┼Ыvya and Preс╣Зi [?]тАФwith those forms of help come here, o A┼Ыvins.

Jamison Brereton Notes

atharv─л╠Б- as тАШden Weg verfolgendтАЩ from Hoffmann (see EWA I.805 and Scarlatta 496-97). GeldnerтАЩs тАЬpfeilschnelle (?)тАЭ is distinctly odd, and I donтАЩt know the basis for his interpr.

Griffith

Wherewith ye helped, in battle of a thousand spoils, Vispala seeking booty, powerless to move.
Wherewith ye guarded friendly Vasa, Asva’s son,–Come hither unto us, O Asvins, with those aids.

Geldner

Mit denen ihr die Vispala, die preisgewinnende, pfeilschnelle, in dem Wettkampf um Tausend als Kampfpreis erquicket, mit denen ihr dem Vasa Asva, dem Preni beistandet, mit diesen Hilfen kommt doch ja her, ihr Asvin!

Grassmann

Durch die ihr halft im tausendfach verschlungnen Kampf der Vi├зpala, der gabenreichen Priesterin, Durch die dem lieben Va├зa A├зvia ihr halft, mit solchen H├╝lfen kommt, o Ritter, schnell herbei.

Elizarenkova

English translation:

тАЬWith those aids by which, beauteous donors, the cloud (was made to) shed its sweet (water), for the sake of the merchant D─лrgha┼Ыravas, the son of Uс╣гij, and by which you protected the devout Kakс╣г─лvat; with them, A┼Ыvins, come willingly hither.тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

D─лrgha┼Ыravas, a с╣Ыс╣гi, was the son of D─лrghatamas; in a time of famine, he became a trader to obtain a livelihood, hence he was a vaс╣Зik a merchant, too

Jamison Brereton

Those through which, o you of good drops, a cask streamed honey for D─лrgha┼Ыravas Au┼Ыija the merchant,
with which you helped Kakс╣г─лvant the praiserтАФwith those forms of help come here, o A┼Ыvins.

Jamison Brereton Notes

Kakс╣г─лvant is the next poet in the collection after Kutsa. HeтАЩs explicitly identified as an Au┼Ыija in I.18.1 and by implication in I.119.9, 122.4-5. What the merchant (vaс╣З├нj-) is doing here I have no idea.

Griffith

Whereby the cloud, ye Bounteous Givers, shed sweet rain for Dirghasravas, for the merchant Ausija,
Wherewith ye helped Kaksivan, singer of your praise,–Come hither unto us, O Asvins, with those aids.

Jamison Brereton

Those with which you swelled the Ras─Б (River) with a gush of water, with which you helped the horseless chariot to victory,

Griffith

Wherewith ye made Rasa swell full with water-floods, and urged to victory the car without a horse;
Wherewith Trisoka drove forth his recovered cows,–Come hither unto us, O Asvins, with those aids.

рд╣реЗ рдЕрд╢реНрд╡рд┐рдиреМ рдкрд░рд╛рд╡рддрд┐ рджреВрд░рджреЗрд╢реЗ рд╕реНрдерд┐рддрдВ рд╕реВрд░реНрдпрдВ рддрдореЛрд░реВрдкреЗрдг рд╕реНрд╡рд░реНрднрд╛рдиреБрдирд╛рд╡реГрддрдорд╛рджрд┐рддреНрдпрдВ рддрд╕реНрдорд╛рддреНрддрдорд╕реЛ рдореЛрдЪрдпрд┐рддреБрдВ рдпрд╛рднрд┐рдГ рдКрддрд┐рднрд┐рдГ рдкрд░рд┐рдпрд╛рдердГ рдпреБрд╡рд╛рдВ рдкрд░рд┐рддреЛ рдЧрдЪреНрдЫрдердГ ред рддрдерд╛ рдордиреНрдзрд╛рддрд╛рд░рдореН рдЛрд╖рд┐рдВ рдХреНрд╖реИрддреНрд░рдкрддреНрдпреЗрд╖реБ ред рдХреНрд╖реЗрддреНрд░рд╛рдгрд╛рдВ рдкрддрд┐рд░рдзрд┐рдкрддрд┐рдГ рдХреНрд╖реЗрддреНрд░рдкрддрд┐рдГ ред рддрддреНрд╕рдВрдмрдиреНрдзрд┐рд╖реБ рдХрд░реНрдорд╕реБ рдЖрд╡рддрдореН рдЕрд░рдХреНрд╖рддрдореН ред рдЕрдкрд┐ рдЪ рдпрд╛рднрд┐рдГ рдКрддрд┐рднрд┐рдГ рд╡рд┐рдкреНрд░рдВ рдореЗрдзрд╛рд╡рд┐рдирдВ рднрд░рджреНрд╡рд╛рдЬрдореН рдЛрд╖рд┐рдордиреНрдирдкреНрд░рджрд╛рдиреЗрди рдкреНрд░ рдЖрд╡рддрдВ рдкреНрд░рдХрд░реНрд╖реЗрдгрд╛рд░рдХреНрд╖рддрдореН ред рддрд╛рднрд┐рдГ рд╕рд░реНрд╡рд╛рднрд┐рдГ рдКрддрд┐рднрд┐рдГ рд╕рд╣ рд░рдХреНрд╖рдгрд╛рд░реНрдердорд╕реНрдорд╛рдирдкреНрдпрд╛рдЧрдЪреНрдЫрддрдореН ред рдХреНрд╖реИрддреНрд░рдкрддреНрдпреЗрд╖реБ ред рдмреНрд░рд╛рд╣реНрдордгрд╛рджреЗрд░рд╛рдХреГрддрд┐рдЧрдгрддреНрд╡рд╛рддреН рдХрд░реНрдордгреНрдпрд░реНрдереЗ рдкреНрдпрдЮреН рее

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬWith those aids by which you encompassed the sun, when afar off, (to extricate him from eclipse); by which you defended Mandh─Бt─Б in (the discharge of) his soverign functions, and by whciс╕е you protected the sage Bharadv─Бja; with them, A┼Ыvins, come willingly hither.тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

Mandh─Бt─Б was a r─Бjaс╣Ыс╣гi, a royal sage. M─Бndh─Бtr─Б is a celebrated prince of the solar dynasty (Viс╣гnu Pur─Бс╣Зa, 363);

Kс╣гetrapati = lord, either of fields or of the earth. Bharadv─Бja, vipra = br─Бhmaс╣Зa, medh─Бvin, wise (Viс╣гnu Pur─Бс╣Зa 449)

Jamison Brereton

Those with which you drive around the sun in the distance and you helped Mandh─Бtar [/the thinker] in (the battles for) lordship of lands, with which you helped the inspired poet Bharadv─БjaтАФwith those forms of help come here, o A┼Ыvins.

Griffith

Wherewith ye, compass round the Sun when far away, strengthened Mandhatar in his tasks as lord of lands,
And to sage Bharadvaja gave protecting help,–Come hither unto us, O Asvins, with those aids.

рджрдпрд╛рдирдиреНрдж-рд╕рд░рд╕реНрд╡рддреА (рд╣рд┐) - рднрд╛рд╡рд╛рд░реНрдердГ

рднрд╛рд╡рд╛рд░реНрдерднрд╛рд╖рд╛рдГ - рд╡реНрдпрд╡рд╣рд╛рд░ рдХрд░рдиреЗрд╡рд╛рд▓реЗ рдордиреБрд╖реНрдпреЛрдВ рд╕реЗ рд╡рд┐рдорд╛рдирд╛рджрд┐ рдпрд╛рдиреЛрдВ рдХреЗ рд╡рд┐рдирд╛ рджреВрд╕рд░реЗ рджреЗрд╢реЛрдВ рдореЗрдВ рдЬрд╛рдирд╛-рдЖрдирд╛ рдирд╣реАрдВ рд╣реЛ рд╕рдХрддрд╛, рдЗрд╕рд╕реЗ рдмрдбрд╝рд╛ рд▓рд╛рдн рдирд╣реАрдВ рд╣реЛ рд╕рдХрддрд╛ред рдЗрд╕ рдХрд╛рд░рдг рдирд╛рд╡-рд╡рд┐рдорд╛рдирд╛рджрд┐ рдХреА рд░рдЪрдирд╛ рдЕрд╡рд╢реНрдп рд╕рджрд╛ рдХрд░рдиреА рдЪрд╛рд╣рд┐рдпреЗ рее резрей рее

рджрдпрд╛рдирдиреНрдж-рд╕рд░рд╕реНрд╡рддреА (рд╣рд┐) - рдЕрдиреНрд╡рдпрдГ

рдЕрдиреНрд╡рдп: рд╣реЗ рдЕрд╢реНрд╡рд┐рдирд╛ рд╢рд┐рд▓реНрдкрд╡рд┐рджреНрдпрд╛рд╕реНрд╡рд╛рдорд┐рднреГрддреНрдпреМ рдпреБрд╡рд╛рдВ рдпрд╛рднрд┐рд░реВрддрд┐рднрд┐рдГ рдкрд░рд╛рд╡рддрд┐ рд╕реВрд░реНрдпрдорд┐рд╡ рдордиреНрдзрд╛рддрд╛рд░рдВ рдкрд░реНрдпрд╛рдердГред рдпрд╛рднрд┐рдГ рдХреНрд╖реИрддреНрд░рдкрддреНрдпреЗрд╖реБ рддрдорд╛рд╡рддрдВ рднрд░рджреНрд╡рд╛рдЬрдВ рд╡рд┐рдкреНрд░рдВ рдЪ рдкреНрд░рд╛рд╡рддрдВ рддрд╛рднрд┐рд░реБ рд╕реНрд╡рд╛рдЧрддрдореН рее резрей рее

рджрдпрд╛рдирдиреНрдж-рд╕рд░рд╕реНрд╡рддреА (рд╣рд┐) - рд╡рд┐рд╖рдпрдГ

рдкреБрдирд╕реНрддреМ рдХрд╛рд╡рд┐рд╡ рдХрд┐рдВ рдХреБрд░реНрдпрд╛рддрд╛рдорд┐рддреНрдпреБрдкрджрд┐рд╢реНрдпрддреЗ ред

рдкрджрд╛рд░реНрдерд╛рдиреНрд╡рдпрднрд╛рд╖рд╛рдГ - (рдпрд╛рднрд┐рдГ) (рд╕реВрд░реНрдпреНрдпрдореН) рдкреНрд░рдХрд╛рд╢рдордпрдореН (рдкрд░рд┐рдпрд╛рдердГ) рд╕рд░реНрд╡рддрдГ рдкреНрд░рд╛рдкреНрдиреБрддрдореН (рдкрд░рд╛рд╡рддрд┐) рд╡рд┐рдкреНрд░рдХреГрд╖реНрдЯреЗ рдорд╛рд░реНрдЧреЗ (рдордиреНрдзрд╛рддрд╛рд░рдореН) рдпрд╛рдиреЗрди рд╕рджреНрдпреЛ рджреВрд░рджреЗрд╢рдВ рдЧрдордпрд┐рддрд╛рд░рдВ рдореЗрдзрд╛рд╡рд┐рдирдореНред рдордиреНрдзрд╛рддреЗрддрд┐ рдореЗрдзрд╛рд╡рд┐рдирд╛режред рдирд┐рдШрдВреж рейред резрелред (рдХреНрд╖реИрддреНрд░рдкрддреНрдпреЗрд╖реБ) рдХреНрд╖реЗрддреНрд░рд╛рдгрд╛рдВ рднреВрдордгреНрдбрд▓рд╛рдирд╛рдВ рдкрддрдпрдГ рдкрд╛рд▓рдХрд╛рд╕реНрддреЗрд╖рд╛рдВ рдХрд░реНрдорд╕реБ (рдЖрд╡рддрдореН) рд░рдХреНрд╖рддрдореН (рдпрд╛рднрд┐рдГ) рд░рдХреНрд╖рд╛рднрд┐рдГ (рд╡рд┐рдкреНрд░рдореН) рдореЗрдзрд╛рд╡рд┐рдирдореН (рдкреНрд░) (рднрд░рджреНрд╡рд╛рдЬрдореН) рд╡рд┐рджреНрдпрд╛рд╕рджреНрдЧреБрдгрд╛рдиреН рднрд░рддрд╛рдВ рд╡рд╛рдЬрдВ рд╡рд┐рдЬреНрдЮрд╛рдкрдпрд┐рддрд╛рд░рдореН (рдЖрд╡рддрдореН) рд╡рд┐рдЬрд╛рдиреАрддрдореНред рдЕрдиреНрдпрддреНрдкреВрд░реНрд╡рд╡рддреН рее резрей рее

рджрдпрд╛рдирдиреНрдж-рд╕рд░рд╕реНрд╡рддреА (рд╣рд┐) - рднрд╛рд╡рд╛рд░реНрдердГ

English translation:

тАЬWith those aids by which you defended the mighty and hospitable Divod─Бsa, (when, having undertaken) the death of ┼Ъambara, he hid himself in the water (through fear of the asuras); by which you protected Trasadasyu in war; with them, A┼Ыvins, come willingly hither.тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

Divod─Бsa was a king (Viс╣гс╣Зu Pur─Бс╣Зa, 407); he is called atithigva, the cherisher of guests (atithi); Trasadasyu was the son of Purukutsa (Viс╣гс╣Зu Pur─Бс╣Зa)

Jamison Brereton

Those with which you helped the great Atithigva Ka┼Ыoj┼л and Divod─Бsa at the smiting of ┼Ъambara,
with which you helped Trasadasyu at the stronghold splittingтАФwith those forms of help come here, o A┼Ыvins.

Griffith

Wherewith, when Sambara was slain, ye guarded well great Atithigva, Divodisa, Kasoju,
And Trasadasyu when the forts were shattered down,–Come hither unto us, O Asvins, with those aids.

Geldner

Mit denen ihr dem gro├Яen Atithigva Kasoju Divodasa im Sambara-Kampf beistandet, mit denen ihr dem Trasadasyu bei dem Burgenbrechen beistandet, - mit diesen Hilfen kommt doch ja her, ihr Asvin!

Grassmann

Durch die dem grossen Atithigva, Ka├зodschu und Divodasa wider ├Зambara ihr halft, Dem Trasadasju bei der Burgzerst├╢rung halft, mit solchen H├╝lfen kommt, o Ritter, schnell herbei.

English translation:

тАЬWith those aids by which you preserved Vamra, praised by all around him, when drinking (the dews of the earth); by which you protected Kali when he had taken a wife, and Pс╣Ыthi,when had lost his horse; with them, A┼Ыvins, come willingly hither.тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

Vamra was a с╣Ыс╣гi, the son of Vikh─Бnas;he is called vipip─Бnam, drinking much and variously, earthly moisture or dew, p─Бrthivam rasam. Kali was a с╣Ыс╣гi and Pс╣Ыthi was a r─Бjaс╣Ыс╣гi

Jamison Brereton

Those with which you favor Vamra [/the ant], who drinks up, and Upastuta, with which you favor Kali, who acquired a wife,
with which you helped Vya┼Ыva and Pr╠еthiтАФwith those forms of help come here, o A┼Ыvins.

Jamison Brereton Notes

On the lexeme medial v├н тИЪp─Б тАШextract by drinking, separate fluids by drinkingтАЩ see disc. ad VII.22.4. Why this lexeme is used here of an ant (or someone so called) isnтАЩt clear. Perhaps it reflects a folk belief or observation about the eating/drinking habits of ants. Popular Science Monthly (of May 1877) reports that тАЬSome speciesтАФsuch, for instance, as the small brown garden antтАФascend bushes in search of aphides. The ant then taps the aphis gently with her antenn├ж, and the aphis emits a drop of sweet fluid, which the ant drinks.тАЭ This could possibly be considered extraction. And a more recent article (Smithsonian.com, Aug. 16, 2012) has photographs of transparent Indian ants whose abdomens change color depending on the color of what they drink. The photographs of the antsтАЩ mouth parts attempting to penetrate drops of colored water could also be viewed as extraction.

Griffith

Wherewith ye honoured the great drinker Vamra, and Upastuta and Kali when he gained his wife,
And lent to Vyasva and to Prthi favouring help,–Come hither unto us, O Asvins, with those aids.

Durch die den Trinker Vamra, den Upastuta, durch die den Kali, als er freite, ihr erquickt, Durch die den Prithi und Via├зva ihr gesch├╝tzt, mit solchen H├╝lfen kommt, o Ritter, schnell herbei.

рджрдпрд╛рдирдиреНрдж-рд╕рд░рд╕реНрд╡рддреА (рд╣рд┐) - рдЕрдиреНрд╡рдпрдГ

рджрдпрд╛рдирдиреНрдж-рд╕рд░рд╕реНрд╡рддреА (рд╣рд┐) - рд╡рд┐рд╖рдпрдГ

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬWith those aids, leaders (of sacrifices), which you afforded to ┼Ъayu, to Atri, and formerly to Manu, anxious (to show them) the way (to escape from evil); with those by which you shot arrows (upon the foes) of Sy┼лmara┼Ыmi; with them, A┼Ыvis, willingly come hither.тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

G─Бtum iс╣гathuс╕е, you wishem to go (out of evil or danger). Manu was a r─Бjaс╣Ыс╣гi, whom the A┼Ыvins extricated from want, by teaching him the art of sowing seeds of barley and other grains. Sy┼лmara┼Ыmi was a с╣Ыс╣гi

Jamison Brereton

Those with which, o superior men, you sought a way for ┼Ъayu, with which for Atri, with which for Manu long ago,
with which you drove the (cows?) of ┼Ъara for Sy┼лmar┼ЫmiтАФwith those forms of help come here, o A┼Ыvins.

Jamison Brereton Notes

┼Ъyumar┼Ыmi in the published translation is a typo for ┼Ъyumara┼Ыmi.

Griffith

Wherewith, O Heroes, ye vouchsafed deliverance to Sayu, Atri, and to Manu long ago;
Wherewith ye shot your shafts in Syumarasmi’s cause.–Come hither unto us, O Asvins, with those aids.

Geldner

Mit denen ihr Herren f├╝r Sayu, mit denen ihr f├╝r Atri, mit denen ihr vormals f├╝r Manu einen Weg suchtet, mit denen ihr dem Syumarasmi die K├╝he des Sara zutriebt, - mit diesen Hilfen kommt doch ja her, ihr Asvin!

Grassmann

Durch welche ihr dem ├Зaju und dem Atri einst, durch die dem Manu ihr zu hohem Gl├╝ck verhalft, Durch die dem Sjumara├зmi Pfeile ihr gebracht, mit solchen H├╝lfen kommt, o Ritter, schnell herbei.

English translation:

тАЬWIth those aids by which Paddarvan shone with with strngth of orm in battle, like a blazing fire piled up (with fuel); by which you defended ┼Ъary─Бta in war; with them, A┼Ыvins, come willingly hither.тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

Paddarvan was a r─Бjaс╣Ыс╣гi;

┼Ъary─Бta = ┼Ъary─Бti, fourth son of Vaivasvata Manu (Viс╣гс╣Зu Pur─Бс╣Зa)

Jamison Brereton

Those with which Paс╣нharvan, with the might of his belly, shone like a fire laid and kindled, on his drive,
with which you help ┼Ъary─Бta in (the contest) for great stakesтАФwith
those forms of help come here, o A┼Ыvins.

Jamison Brereton Notes

Note the phonological play in p├бс╣нharv─Б j├бс╣нharasya. Because of its accent, Geldner (/Witzel Got┼Н) take j├бс╣нhara- as an adjectival deriv. of jaс╣нh├бra- тАШbellyтАЩ, hence тАШpaunchyтАЩ (supposedly of his wagon). But I think it likely that its accent simply follows its phonological twin p├бс╣нharv─Б, which immediately precedes (see also Oldenberg). The only possible indication of the independent existence of j├бс╣нhara- is j├бс╣нhala- in I.182.6.

Griffith

Wherewith Patharva, in his majesty of form, shone in his course like to a gathered kindled fire;
Wherewith ye helped Saryata in the mighty fray,–Come hither unto us, O Asvins, with those aids.

Geldner

Mit denen Patharvan kraft seines bauchigen Wagens wie geschichtetes entz├╝ndetes Feuer leuchtete in der Rennbahn, mit denen ihr dem Saryata beistandet im Kampf um den gro├Яen Siegerpreis, - mit diesen Hilfen kommt doch ja her, ihr Asvin!

Grassmann

Durch die Patharvan strahlte, m├дchtig von Gestalt, auf seinem Zug, wie Feuer, das geschichtet flammt, Durch die ihr dem ├Зarjata halft im grossen Kampf, mit solchen H├╝lfen kommt, o Ritter, schnell herbei.

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬAс╣Еgiras, (prise the A┼Ыvins); A┼Ыvins, with those aids by which, with (gratified) minds, you delight (in praise), and thence preceded the gods to the cavern, to recover the stolen cattle; by which you sustained the heroic Manu with food; with them, A┼Ыvins, come willingly hither.тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

Sustained Manu: By making him aware of the grain hidden in the earth, or teaching him, in fact, agriculture

Jamison Brereton

Those by which, o Aс╣Еgiras, with your mind you two *find a way out and go to the forefront at the opening up of (the cave) flooding with cows,
with which you helped Manu the champion with refreshmentтАФwith those forms of help come here, o A┼Ыvins.

Jamison Brereton Notes

The problem of the sg. voc. aс╣Еgiraс╕е is treated by Oldenberg

The verb niraс╣Зy├бthaс╕е is also problematic; in fact Geldner declines to tr. it. Renou suggests that it might be a corruption of *ni(r)-riс╣З─лthaс╕е to n├нr тИЪr─л тАШlet flow, let escapeтАЩ, but the corruption involved would have to be fairly massive and would be unmotivated. Oldenberg sees it as a denom. to a form derived from тИЪran тАШtake pleasureтАЩ.

Witzel Got┼Н tr. тАЬihr тАж innerlich Freude habt,тАЭ following Got┼Н 1987: 258 n. 582, who accepts GrassmannтАЩs connection with тИЪran тАШtake pleasureтАЩ, though he attributes the accentuation not to a passive stem raс╣Зy├б- (as Grassmann does, despite the active ending) but to a shift from the standard pres. stem r├бс╣Зya- by association with denominatives like turaс╣Зy├б- (or perhaps to its being a denominative itself). This analysis is accepted by Kulikov (Vedic -ya-presents, pp. 605-5), with further discussion. Although a connection with тИЪran makes more sense than RenouтАЩs suggestion, it does not make much sense in context – or rather, although the tr. is harmless and not jarring, it has nothing to do with the Vala myth treated in the following p─Бda. It is also the case that тИЪran does not otherwise occur with n├н and forms of this root are also almost always construed with a source from which the pleasure is derived. By contrast, my tr. follows a suggestion of BreretonтАЩs that it is haplologized from *nirayaс╣Зa-y├б- тАШseek/find a way out’. Despite the further machinery required, this interpr. makes more sense in the Vala myth context.

Griffith

Wherewith, Angirases! ye triumphed in your heart, and onward went to liberate the flood of milk;
Wherewith ye helped the hero Manu with new strength,–Come hither unto us, O Asvins, with those aids.

Mit denen ihr, o Angiras, von Herzen …….und voranginget in dem Spalt der Bergh├╢hle, die die Rindermasse barg, durch die ihr dem tapferen Manu mit Nahrung aushalft, - mit diesen Hilfen kommt doch ja her, ihr Asvin!

Grassmann

Mit denen ihr, o Angira’s, euch gern erfreut, und vorw├дrts zu der rinderreichen Grotte eilt, Durch die dem Helden Manu ihr zum Trank verhalft, mit solchen H├╝lfen kommt, o Ritter, schnell herbei.

English translation:

тАЬWith those aids by which you gave a wife to Vimada, by which you recovered the ruddy kine, by which you conferred excellent wealth upon Sud─Бs; with them, A┼Ыvins, come willingly hither.тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

Purumitra’s daughter was obtained as a wife for the с╣Ыс╣гi Vimada;

Sud─Бs: name of a king, son of Pijavana. Paijavana, son of Pijavana is noted (Manu, 8.110)

Jamison Brereton

Those with which you brought home wives for Vimada or with which you did your best to obtain the ruddy (cows),
with which you brought Sudev─л (as wife) [/divine favor] for Sud─БsтАФwith those forms of help come here, o A┼Ыvins.

Griffith

Wherewith ye brought a wife for Vimada to wed, wherewith ye freely gave the ruddy cows away;
Wherewith ye brought the host of kind Gods to Sudas–Come hither unto us, O Asvins, with those aids.

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬWith those aids by which you are bestowers of happiness upon the donor (of oblations), by which you have protected Bhujyu and Adhrigu, and by which you have granted delighting and nourishing (food) to Ritastubh; with them. A┼Ыvins, come willingly hither.тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

Adhrigu was a sacrificer, immolator, along with Capa, of the gods: adhrigus capas ca dev─Бn─Бm ┼Ыamit─Бrau (Taittir─лya Br─Бhmaс╣Зa 3.6.6.4; с╣Ъtastubh was a с╣Ыс╣гi

Jamison Brereton

Those with which you become weal for the pious man, with which you aid Bhujyu, with which Adhrigu,
(and make) (the woman) R╠еtastubh comfortable and easy-bearingтАФwith those forms of help come here, o A┼Ыvins.

Jamison Brereton Notes

The problem in these obscure fragments of tales is to decide which of the words are PNs and which are adjs. In c Geldner takes the three fem. acc. as separate names, but I prefer to take omiy─Б╠Бvat─лm and subh├бr─Бm as proleptic adjectives, since both stems are found earlier in the hymn in full lexical usage (omy─Б╠Бvantam 7b, subh├бr─Б(с╕е) 2a). Sim. Scarlatta (p. 639), Remmer (Frauennamen, p. 85).

Griffith

Wherewith ye bring great bliss to him who offers gifts, wherewith ye have protected Bhujyu, Adhrigu,
And good and gracious Subhara and Rtastup,–Come hither unto us, O Asvins, with those aids.

Geldner

Mit denen ihr dem Opferspender heilbringend seid, mit denen ihr dem Bhujyu beisteht, mit denen dem Adhrigu, mit denen ihr der Omyavati, der Subhara, der Ritastubh beigestanden habt, - mit diesen Hilfen kommt doch ja her, ihr Asvin!

Grassmann

Durch die ihr segnet den, der euch gehuldigt hat, durch die ihr helft dem Bhudschju und dem Adhrigu, Der Subhara, der holden und dem Ritastubh, mit solchen H├╝lfen kommt, o Ritter, schnell herbei.

Elizarenkova

рд╕реНрд╡рд╛рдирд╛рджрд┐рд╖реБ рд╕реЛрдордкрд╛рд▓реЗрд╖реБ’ рдордзреНрдпреЗ рдХреГрд╢рд╛рдиреБрд░реЗрдХрдГ рд╕реЛрдордкрд╛рд▓рдГ ред рддрдерд╛ рдЪ рддреИрддреНрддрд┐рд░реАрдпрдХрдВ- рд╣рд╕реНрдд рд╕реБрд╣рд╕реНрдд рдХреГрд╢рд╛рдирд╡реЗрддреЗ рд╡рдГ рд╕реЛрдордХреНрд░рдпрдгрдГ: ’ (рддреИ. рд╕рдВ. рез. реи.рен) рдЗрддрд┐ ред рддрдВ рдХреГрд╢рд╛рдиреБрдореН рдЕрд╕рдиреЗред рдЗрд╖рд╡реЛрд╜рд╕реНрдпрдиреНрддреЗрд╜рд╕реНрдорд┐рдиреНрдирд┐рддреНрдпрд╕рдирдГ рд╕рдВрдЧреНрд░рд╛рдордГ ред рддрд╕реНрдорд┐рдиреН рд╕рдВрдЧреНрд░рд╛рдореЗ рд╣реЗ рдЕрд╢реНрд╡рд┐рдиреМ рдпрд╛рднрд┐рдГ рдКрддрд┐рднрд┐рдГ рджреБрд╡рд╕реНрдпрдердГ рд░рдХреНрд╖рдердГ ред рддрдерд╛ рдпрд╛рднрд┐рдГ рдЪ рдЬрд╡реЗ рд╡реЗрдЧреЗ рдкреНрд░рд╡реГрддреНрддрдВ рдпреВрдирдГ рддрд░реБрдгрд╕реНрдп рдкреБрд░реБрдХреБрддреНрд╕рд╕реНрдп рдЕрд░реНрд╡рдиреНрддрдореН рдЕрд╢реНрд╡рдореН рдЖрд╡рддрдореН рдЕрд░рдХреНрд╖рддрдореН ред рдЕрдкрд┐ рдЪ рдпрддреН рдордзреБ рдХреНрд╖реМрджреНрд░рдВ рдкреНрд░рд┐рдпрдВ рд╕рд░реНрд╡реЗрд╖рд╛рдордиреБрдХреВрд▓рд╡реЗрджреНрдпрдВ рддрддреН рд╕рд░рдбреНрднреНрдпрдГ рдордзреБрдордХреНрд╖рд┐рдХрд╛рднреНрдпрдГ рдпрд╛рднрд┐рдГ рдЪ рдКрддрд┐рднрд┐рдГ рднрд░рдердГ рд╕рдВрдкрд╛рджрдпрдердГ ред рддрд╛рднрд┐рдГ рд╕рд░реНрд╡рд╛рднрд┐рдГ рдКрддрд┐рднрд┐рдГ рд╕рд╣рд╛рд╕реНрдорд╛рдирдкреНрдпрд╛рдЧрдЪреНрдЫрддрдореН рее рдЕрд╕рдиреЗ ред тАШрдЕрд╕реБ рдХреНрд╖реЗрдкрдгреЗ ’ ред ’ рдХрд░рдгрд╛рдзрд┐рдХрд░рдгрдпреЛрд╢реНрдЪ ’ рдЗрддрд┐ рдЕрдзрд┐рдХрд░рдгреЗ рд▓реНрдпреБрдЯреН ред рд╕рд░рдбреНрднреНрдпрдГ ред тАШрд╕реГ рдЧрддреМ ред рд╕рд░реНрддреЗрд░рдЯрд┐рдГ рее

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬWith those aids by which you defended Kс╣Ы┼Ы─Бnu in battle, with which you succoured the horse of the young Purukutsa in speed, and by which you deliver the plural asant honey to the bees; with them, A┼Ыvins, come willingly hither.тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

Kс╣Ы┼Ы─Бnu are somap─Бlas, vendors or providers of Soma; hasta-suhasta-kс╣Ы┼Ы─Бnavaс╕е, te vaс╕е somakrayaс╣Зaс╕е (Taittir─лya Saс╣Гhit─Б 1.2.7);

Kс╣Ы┼Ы─Бnu = agni; purukutsa was the son of Mandh─Бt─Б and husband of Narmad─Б, the river; the text has only ‘of the young’, Purukutsa is added

Jamison Brereton

With which you favor Kr╠е┼Ы─Бnu in shooting, with which you helped the steed of the youth in speedтАФ
you bring the dear honey that comes from the beesтАФwith those forms of help come here, o A┼Ыvins.

Jamison Brereton Notes

P─Бda c presents a major disruption of the pattern that has monotonously structured this hymn since vs. 5; this disruption may signal the approaching end of the hymn. Unlike every c-p─Бda in the hymn (starting indeed with vs. 1) save for the immediately preceding one, the p─Бda doesnтАЩt begin with y─Б╠Бbhiс╕е (11c doesnтАЩt actually begin with y─Б╠Бbhiс╕е, but it is found within the p─Бda). Moreover the verb bharathaс╕е is not accented and therefore cannot be in even a notional relative clause, despite the y├бd that immediately follows it. Curiously, most interpr. ignore or explain away these deviations. Geldner tr. as a тАЬwennтАЭ clause and considers y├бd тАЬAttraktion f├╝r y─Б╠Бbhiс╕етАЭ (attraction to what he doesnтАЩt say). Oldenberg ascribes y├бd for y─Б╠Бbhiс╕е to metrical needs and wishes to accent bharathaс╕е, because switching to a main clause is тАЬrecht unwahrscheinlich.тАЭ Since the poet clearly had no problem maintaining his template in verse after verse, I find it impossible to believe that the departures from this structure here are not deliberate – a kind of putting on the brakes before the end, just as the full template took awhile to take shape at the beginning of the hymn. More recent tr. reflect the verseтАЩs structure better: Witzel Got┼Н make c a parenthetical clause (though, oddly, repeating the тАЬattractionтАЭ explan. in the n.); Scarlatta (p. 444) also treats the clause as parenthetical.

The formally ambiguous sar├бс╕Нbhyaс╕е is taken by Geldner (/Witzel Got┼Н) as dative, but given real-world knowledge – bees produce honey and donтАЩt need it brought to them

– it surely makes better sense as an ablative (so also L├╝ders, Scarlatta.), in what looks almost like an izafe construction: y├бt sar├бс╕Нbhyaс╕е.

Griffith

Wherewith ye served Krsanu where the shafts were shot, and helped the young man’s horse to swiftness in the race;
Wherewith ye bring delicious honey to the bees,–Come hither unto us, O Asvins, with those aids.

Wherewith ye, Lords of Hundred Powers, helped Kutsa, son of Arjuni, gave Turviti and Dabhiti strength,
Favoured Dhvasanti and lent Purusanti help,–Come hither unto us, O Asvins, with those aids.

рджрдпрд╛рдирдиреНрдж-рд╕рд░рд╕реНрд╡рддреА (рд╣рд┐) - рдЕрдиреНрд╡рдпрдГ

рдЕрдиреНрд╡рдп: рд╣реЗ рд╢рддрдХреНрд░рддреВ рдЕрд╢реНрд╡рд┐рдирд╛ рд╕рднрд╛рд╕реЗрдиреЗрд╢реМ рдпреБрд╡рд╛рдВ рдпрд╛рднрд┐рд░реВрддрд┐рднрд┐рдГ рд╕реВрд░реНрдпрдЪрдиреНрджреНрд░рд╡рддреН рдкреНрд░рдХрд╛рд╢рдорд╛рдиреМ рд╕рдиреНрддрд╛рд╡рд╛рд░реНрдЬреБрдиреЗрдпрдВ рдХреБрддреНрд╕рдВ рд╕рдВрдЧреГрд╣реНрдп рддреБрд░реНрд╡реАрддрд┐рдВ рджрднреАрддрд┐рдВ рдзреНрд╡рд╕рдиреНрддрд┐рдВ рдкреНрд░рд╛рд╡рддрдореНред рдпрд╛рднрд┐рдГ рдкреБрд░реБрд╖рдиреНрддрд┐рдВ рдЪ рдкреНрд░рд╛рд╡рддрдВ рддрд╛рднрд┐рд░реБ рдзрд░реНрдордВ рд░рдХреНрд╖рд┐рддреБрдВ рд╕реНрд╡рд╛рдЧрддрдореН рее реирей рее

рджрдпрд╛рдирдиреНрдж-рд╕рд░рд╕реНрд╡рддреА (рд╣рд┐) - рд╡рд┐рд╖рдпрдГ

рдЕрде рддреЗ рджреБрд╖реНрдЯрдирд┐рд╡реГрддреНрддрд┐рдВ рд╢реНрд░реЗрд╖реНрдард░рдХреНрд╖рд╛рдВ рдХрдердВ рдХреБрд░реНрдпреНрдпреБрд░рд┐рддреНрдпрд╛рд╣ ред

English translation:

тАЬA┼Ыvins, sanctify our words with works; showerers (of benefits), subduers of foes (invigorate) our understandin g(for the sacred study); we invoke you both, in the last watch of the night, for our preservation; be to us for increase in the provision of food.тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

Ady┼лtye, in the absense of light, i.e. in the last watch of the night, or that preceding the dawn, at which time, according to ─А┼Ыval─Бyana ┼Ъrauta S┼лtra, the A┼Ыvins are especially to be worshipped

Make speech fruitful for us, o A┼Ыvins; make for us inspired thought, o wondrous bulls.
I call you down for help at a time when one shouldnтАЩt gamble. Be there to strengthen us at the winning of prizes.

рдкрджрд╛рд░реНрдерд╛рдиреНрд╡рдпрднрд╛рд╖рд╛рдГ - (рджреНрдпреБрднрд┐рдГ) рджрд┐рд╡рд╕реИрдГ (рдЕрдХреНрддреБрднрд┐рдГ) рд░рд╛рддреНрд░рд┐рднрд┐рдГ рд╕рд╣ рд╡рд░реНрддреНрддрдорд╛рдирд╛рдиреН (рдкрд░рд┐) рд╕рд░реНрд╡рддрдГ (рдкрд╛рддрдореН) рд░рдХреНрд╖рддрдореН (рдЕрд╕реНрдорд╛рдиреН) рднрд╡рджрд╛рд╢реНрд░рд┐рддрд╛рдиреН (рдЕрд░рд┐рд╖реНрдЯреЗрднрд┐рдГ) рд╣рд┐рдВрд╕рд┐рддреБрдордирд░реНрд╣реИрдГ (рдЕрд╢реНрд╡рд┐рдирд╛) (рд╕реМрднрдЧреЗрднрд┐рдГ) рд╢реЛрднрдиреИрд╢реНрд╡рд░реНрдпреИрдГ (рддрддреН) (рдирдГ) (рдорд┐рддреНрд░рдГ) (рд╡рд░реБрдгрдГ) (рдорд╛рдорд╣рдиреНрддрд╛рдореН) (рдЕрджрд┐рддрд┐рдГ) (рд╕рд┐рдиреНрдзреБрдГ) (рдкреГрдерд┐рд╡реА) (рдЙрдд) (рджреНрдпреМрдГ) рдПрд╖рд╛рдВ рдкреВрд░реНрд╡рд╡рджрд░реНрдердГ рее реирел рее

рджрдпрд╛рдирдиреНрдж-рд╕рд░рд╕реНрд╡рддреА (рд╣рд┐) - рднрд╛рд╡рд╛рд░реНрдердГ

рд╕рд╡рд┐рддрд╛ рдЬреЛрд╢реА тЖР рджрдпрд╛рдирдиреНрдж-рд╕рд░рд╕реНрд╡рддреА (рдо) - рднрд╛рд╡рд╛рд░реНрдердГ

рднрд╛рд╡рд╛рд░реНрдерднрд╛рд╖рд╛рдГ - рдпрд╛ рдордВрддреНрд░рд╛рдд рд╡рд╛рдЪрдХрд▓реБрдкреНрддреЛрдкрдорд╛рд▓рдВрдХрд╛рд░ рдЖрд╣реЗ. рдЬрд╕реЗ рдорд╛рддрд╛рдкрд┐рддрд╛ рдЖрдкрд╛рдкрд▓реНрдпрд╛ рд╕рдВрддрд╛рдирд╛рдВрдирд╛, рд╕рдЦрд╛ рдорд┐рддреНрд░рд╛рдВрдирд╛, рдкреНрд░рд╛рдг рд╢рд░реАрд░рд╛рд▓рд╛ рдкреНрд░рд╕рдиреНрди рдХрд░рддрд╛рдд. рд╕рдореБрджреНрд░ рдЧрдВрднреАрд░рддрд╛, рдкреГрдереНрд╡реА рд╡реГрдХреНрд╖ рд╡ рд╕реВрд░реНрдпрдкреНрд░рдХрд╛рд╢ рдзрд╛рд░рдг рдХрд░реВрди рд╕рд░реНрд╡ рдкреНрд░рд╛рдгреНрдпрд╛рдВрдирд╛ рд╕реБрдЦреА рдХрд░реВрди рдЙрдкрдХрд╛рд░ рдХрд░рддрд╛рдд рддрд╕реЗ рдЕрдзреНрдпрд╛рдкрдХ рд╡ рдЙрдкрджреЗрд╢рдХ рдпрд╛рдВрдиреА рд╕рд░реНрд╡ рд╕рддреНрдп рд╡рд┐рджреНрдпрд╛ рд╡ рдЪрд╛рдВрдЧрд▓реЗ рд╢рд┐рдХреНрд╖рдг рдкреНрд░рд╛рдкреНрдд рдХрд░реВрди рд╕рд░реНрд╡рд╛рдВрдирд╛ рдЗрд╖реНрдЯ рдЕрд╕реЗ рд╕реБрдЦ рджреНрдпрд╛рд╡реЗ. рее реирел рее
